Again most important thing is the entry, some will argue with this. If you don't have a good entry to the market, you give money to the market. second thing we need to learn is patience.  
  
you're trading hourly/H4, you will be waiting for a few days at times to make trades.  
  
"Your paid to wait"  
  
Second the mentality has to be right, your mentality is different to scalping 10/30 pips . will go into the mentality a bit more. because it's vitally important. without it you have no chance. 

It's in fear when people show what they truly value.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar601217_3.gif) hitan234](hitan234)

[Kathy Lien](https://www.investing.com/members/51840) analysis ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f602.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f602.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f602.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f602.png?v=15.1)  
  
  
The biggest driver of currency flows this past week had nothing to do with monetary policy or economic data. Instead, the escalation of tensions between the U.S. and North Korea sent USD/JPY sharply lower as investors worry that this heated exchange could result in military action. Although we firmly believe that the threat of war â let alone nuclear war â is slim, as this era has been one of the most unpredictable in history. Bottom line? Be prepared for the unexpected. Many of our readers are asking how far the dollar could fall if the U.S. goes to war with North Korea but before discussing this, we want to point out that while the dollar is down sharply this week versus the yen, it strengthened against other major currencies like sterling and Australian and New Zealand dollars. So while thereâs no question that war is negative for USD/JPY, it can initially drive the dollar higher against high-beta currencies such as AUD and NZD. As a rule of thumb, the Japanese yen and Swiss franc perform best during times of war, which means all the yen crosses, including USD/JPY, will weaken.  
Taking a look at some of the major military conflicts over the past 3 decades, the Dollar Index suffers greatly when there is war. Not only does the cost of war require an expansion of money supply, commodity prices also tend to rise, putting additional pressure on the U.S. economy. In the 2 months from when the conflicts in Libya started, the Dollar Index dropped nearly 5% while during the first 3 months of the second Gulf War, the index fell more than 9%. We saw similar weakness after the first Gulf War and then later when there were missile attacks on Baghdad. U.S. stocks tend to perform poorly, though generally during the month before war begins rather than the month after. This time around, how currencies behave depends largely on how China responds. If China stays neutral and doesnât provide any support to North Korea, the yen, Australian and New Zealand dollars will have a smaller reaction (although still a big one) than if China inserts itself in the conflict. Since thereâs no doubt that North Korea will lose and lose quickly, as the tensions grow the dollar will suffer and the actual announcement of war could take USD/JPY to 105. But if a swift victory transpired, the pair would recover quickly. The bottom line is that the outlook for USD/JPY is grim and 108.50/108.00 is probably the next stop for the pair.  
Aside from the threat of war, U.S. data has been far from impressive with jobless claims rising as inflationary pressures remain subdued. Monetary policy committee members arenât happy with the current state of inflation and their feelings are reinforced by the weaker-than-expected consumer- and producer-price reports. According to Fed President Dudley, it will take some time for inflation to rise to 2% as the weaker dollar affects import prices. As a result, year-over-year price measures will be depressed for a while and the economy may be a bit more sluggish on the margin. Dudley is one of the main architects of Fed policy and his cautious views confirm that the central bank is in no rush to raise interest rates. This sentiment is shared by FOMC voter Evans and Fed President Bullard. Looking ahead, the most important releases on the U.S. calendar will be the FOMC minutes and U.S. retail sales. Although consumer spending could be supported by the rise in wages and rally in stocks, the Fed minutes are likely to be less hawkish as the central bank doesnât seem to want to commit much beyond September balance-sheet normalization.  
Meanwhile, the risk aversion created by U.S./North Korea tensions also put significant pressure on commodity currencies. The New Zealand dollar was the worst performer and more losses are likely in the coming week. According to Governor Wheeler, the Reserve Bank is not happy with the value of the currency as he brought up the possibility of intervention after this monthâs monetary policy announcement. The RBNZ left interest rates unchanged at 1.75% and said inflation could decline further in coming quarters. Wheeler also talked about how currency intervention is always an option. Assistant Governor McDermott emphasized the significance of Wheelerâs comments by saying the RBNZ changed the NZD language to signal their unease â the first step toward possible intervention. The RBNZ opened up a can of worms and next weekâs PMI services, retail sales and producer price reports probably wonât lend much support to the currency, especially after the slowdown in manufacturing PMI index. We see NZD/USD falling back to 0.7250 and possibly even 0.7200.  
Unlike the New Zealand dollar, the Australian dollar quietly drifted lower this past week as the threat of war is positive for gold and commodity prices, which is good for AUD. U.S. Treasury yields also fell more aggressively than Australian bond rates and this change in the yield spread helped to limit the slide in AUD/USD. With that in mind, the Australia

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar470862_13.gif) DrForexMD](drforexmd)

  * Joined Jun 2016 | Status: PA Pivot Swing Trader | [3,892 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=470862)

I agree with the videos that ensale shared and emanuel788 has explained that fundamentals or particular Red News only points to peak times of liquidity and momentum by the Banker/Broker Market Makers against us, the Forex retailers. Also, the notion of having The Edge as per Mark Douglas, that Davits here on his FF thread explains, is there is no guarantee on the direction ever during the major news and usually is opposite to the biased news. The above free videos on youtube regarding retail forex trading and those of Mark Douglas on youtube are worth reviewing to have the right overall mindset as a trader. And of course, the above brilliant quotes of the billionaire Warren Buffet, puts into perspective why only 5 to 10% are consistently successful and make sure you have more than one source of income!

Hi ensale,  
I have been around for sometime on FF Threads here learning from many authors with their Threads and methods. You know, as others here, that you do have a very good LT approach to trading focusing on the double tops and bottoms using the higher H4 and D1 TFs..  
So, do not listen to the negative folks that spring up. You received blessings from emanual7788 himself on your new thread because he sees how you can add value in helping us, the retail Forex traders, to add a supplemental income.  
Stay strong and ignore nonsense from people that would interfere with your objectives to help the rest of us interested in trading on the H4 and Daily TFs.  
I look forward to next week working your approach.  
I do follow and trade the lower TFs on M15 and M30 using Davit's methods and attempt Cigarguy's Fast In Fast Out (FIFO) usng the M1 TF with some good results as well. But, I am interested in using the higher TFs using your approach to reduce my daily stress for my personal heath.  
So, I believe we need you to stay as long as you enjoy what you are doing and not allow your work to interfere with your health.  
Cheers !

Hi Ensale,   
  
I needed some time to study the two pdfs which you shared as well as the three videos and all the nice explanations here in this threat. Thank you for this grate stuff! It's really generous to share this with us.   
  
A few questions now: as I understood the double top or double bottom is the most important part in your strategy. So this is clear. At first: find good looking double tops/bottoms.  
  
Than it's interesting how price respects and rides sometimes the 20 sma. This helps us for entry right? So if I find a double top or bottom I have to wait until price closed over the 20 sma, than wait for the 5/20 crossover (often it happens at the same time)? This is our entry trigger isn't it? So far so easy.   
  
Than the Fibonacci tool. As I understood it would add to probability that the trade will be successful if we find double tops and bottoms at significant fibo lines right? And if we trade h4 time frame we draw the fibo from last month's high to last month's low. Where we draw the fibs for daily time frame or hourly? And which fibo levels are relevant?   
  
Than the videos about stop hunting and tend trading. As I understood it adds to the probability to our trades, if we find for example a double top on h1 after 3 big interweeks waves as well as a stop hunting after this 3 waves. So the stop hunting could be the beginning of the next 3 wave down move right?   
  
Sorry for all the questions ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) but I need to sort all the knowledge a little bit for me to understand the trading plan.   
  
Enjoy your weekend ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

> [Quoting kleybenny](/thread/post/10184602#post10184602 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Ensale, ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)
> 
> Ignored

Great.. We needed someone to ask these question's.. big respect to you for doing it.  
  
Q 1: as I understood the double top or double bottom is the most important part in your strategy. So this is clear. At first: find good looking double tops/bottoms.   
  
A 1: Yes number one, Is finding the best DT/DB, and even better in favourable areas. such as fib retraces etc.  
  
  
Q 2:Then it's interesting how price respects and rides sometimes the 20 sma. This helps us for entry right? So if I find a double top or bottom I have to wait until price closed over the 20 sma, than wait for the 5/20 crossover (often it happens at the same time)? This is our entry trigger isn't it?  
  
A 2: in post 87. I explained and showed an entry with the crossover, in an uptrend and then market turn this type of entry is good, as it's more conservative, whereas in a down trend, I would enter a double top before the crossover. very good question.  
  
  
Q 3: Where we draw the fibs for daily time frame or hourly? And which fibo levels are relevant?   
  
A 3: For hourly, last week high/low + plus the month if you wanted additional areas. but I would stick ... For daily trading. monthly High/low fibs as well as year high/low. ( I will address fibs in more detail soon)   
  
  
Q 4: Then the videos about stop hunting and tend trading. As I understood it adds to the probability to our trades, if we find for example a double top on h1 after 3 big interweeks waves as well as a stop hunting after this 3 waves. So the stop hunting could be the beginning of the next 3 wave down move right? 7  
  
A 4: Yes. correct. as the market is not perfect, it's dynamic but this information helps you identify manipulation. over the year's you get better at it. believe me. so the 3 waves, manipulation won't come into play on every Double top/Double bottom.. However to keep note of it and recognise it helps. Like i show below.  
  
  
GBPAUD.  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 2017-08-13_12h22_20.png
Size: 164 KB](/attachment/image/2437857/thumbnail?d=1502623680)](/attachment/image/2437857?d=1502623680)   

  
  
The double top then has a nice retrace trade but does not begin a 3 step move down. but was rather a retrace trade for the third move up on a bigger 3 wave move. however the information garnered from the video's helped you in this case and will help you as your study continues.  
  
  
.. 

It's in fear when people show what they truly value.

Hi Ensale,  
  
  
Good to see you with your own thread.  
  
I believe it is important to be aware of PRICE in accordance with Whole and Half Numbers.  
  
Banks and Institutions use them for Accumulating and Distributing their positions.  
  
Take a look at the GBP/AUD Chart with Whole and Half Numbers added and see how PRICE behaves around them  
  
Take a look at any Pair and you will see the same thing.

Hi! Correct me if I am wrong, but based on the smart money manipulation videos presented by [Ensale](https://www.forexfactory.com/ensale), we are looking for double tops/bottoms formed with stop loss hunt. So the most recent peak/trough must exceed the previous one by at least one pip (at least 3 pips, according to those three videos).

#  [](/thread/689816-pa-based-ltg)PA based LTG 

  * 

  * [#181](/thread/post/10187485#post10187485 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 14, 2017 9:21pm  Aug 14, 2017 9:21pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar355732_1.gif) ensale](ensale)

  * Joined Nov 2013 | Status: Trader | [2,780 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=355732)

Now I will go into why it works or why it happen's.. the wick above/swing failure setup.  
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 2017-08-14_12h41_12.png
Size: 218 KB](/attachment/image/2438942/thumbnail?d=1502712723)](/attachment/image/2438942?d=1502712723)   

  
  
Buyer's enter and have their buy stops above swing high's in anticipation of a new high, seller's that sold on the down run have their stop above their swing.. Both get twanked by the up move to the swing and above it by 1 pip then down..   
  
More examples coming soon. 

It's in fear when people show what they truly value.

  * Aug 16, 2017 2:52am  Aug 16, 2017 2:52am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar601217_3.gif) hitan234](hitan234)

  * | Membership Revoked  | Joined Aug 2017 | [175 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=601217)

The [US dollar](https://www.investing.com/quotes/us-dollar-index) so far this year has been very week, losing nearly 10% of its value. This decline might have influenced investors to go long the [euro](https://www.investing.com/currencies/eur-usd). Below looks at sentiment toward the euro, which we shared 9 days ago.  
  
  
The chart above reflects that bullish euro sentiment is historically high and in the past when it reached these levels, it was closer to a high than a low.  
Below looks at King Dollarâs pattern over the past couple of years.  
  
  
  
  
USD, while testing 2-year support, also finds itself at the apex of a bullish falling wedge, where two weeks ago at (1) a **large bullish reversal wick (reversal pattern) formed.** This support test is taking place while momentum is oversold and attempting to turn up.  
This week, King Dollar is attempting to breakout above resistance of the bullish falling wedge at (3). A rally in the USD and decline in the euro could put downward pressure on [gold](https://www.investing.com/commodities/gold), [silver](https://www.investing.com/commodities/silver) and the miners.  
Due to this pattern, members went long long the USD near the start of this month, with a stop just below the apex of the bullish falling wedge.

GU..   
  
First chart/ swing high to low on the 4hr. 23.6 retrace and then move to 127.2, no more no less. next charts we bring the month fib's and the confluences.  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 2017-08-15_18h31_58.png
Size: 38 KB](/attachment/image/2441263/thumbnail?d=1502822514)](/attachment/image/2441263?d=1502822514)   

  
  
...  
as mentioned by our star.. dean1star, moves between 50-61.8 fib levels, which are retraces from the up move -- for those that are not aware, GU is being sold at 50% and 61.8 percent cheaper then the gains it made last month, if that explanation helps for those that are new to Fibonacci.   
  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 2017-08-15_18h46_10.png
Size: 133 KB](/attachment/image/2441266/thumbnail?d=1502822585)](/attachment/image/2441266?d=1502822585)   

  
  
Also note on the above chart, we are (were, posted on this yesterday) testing the underside of the 50 % fib. normally a retrace we look for the up move however we tested the underside and didn't break above. also note we running below the 20 EMA on h4.. showing the trend is down.  
  
..   

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: 2017-08-15_19h04_37.png
Size: 101 KB](/attachment/image/2441269/thumbnail?d=1502822812)](/attachment/image/2441269?d=1502822812)   

  
  
This last chart highlight's The confluences and the use of two fib's being drawn. one being the monthly and the other being recent swing high and low on H4.. and reading the double top at the those important level's..  
  
So you've learned how to use the fib's for swings high's/lows + monthly levels. I will post more to cement the ideas shared.. next will post about weekly fib levels and daily for the hourly trading.   
  
  
Questions welcome

Hi Ensale,  
  
Price is drawn to where ever the Pending Orders are placed who ever holds the greater Orders Wins.  
  
The speed of the Bearish move from 1.30000 BRN-1.29500 Level tells me there are more Sellers than Buyers at this Level, for now.  
  
New and existing Sell/Buy Orders will be building at this Level once more.  
  
Chances are we will see Price return to this Level for the Liquidity these Orders provide.  
  
This is as accurate as I can be for now because I don't know where the Orders are placed.

Ensale,  
  
Looks a great thread and method, thanks for sharing. As you can see by my name, I have found you from the other place!  
  
Just a question on the Moving Averages used and the indicators / template you shared.  
  
You specified 20 Simple Moving Average, assuming of the Close?  
  
The Crossover Signal indicator uses 5 EMA and 20 EMA so the signal arrows do not align with crossover of the 20 SMA  
  
So, is that on purpose or the only indicator you found at the time?  
  
For reference, check the Daily of USDCAD to see the big difference in the 20 SMA & 20 EMA  
  
Should it be changed to a 20 EMA on the charts?  
  
All the best, John

Okay here it is, all indicators except Moving Averages, I'm sure your MT4 has those  
  
**WARNING:** the indicator "**2) PVSRA Access Panel (Black)** " requires a certain degree of expertise with MT4. First, there is a "set" file for my settings. However, the time may be wrong in different parts of the world. Please read the instructions, we don't want Ensale's thread to become a support center, thanks.  
  
The magic of that indicator is what you can see on the 1 hour chart, Pivots, session times, round numbers, projected high & low for for daily & weekly   
  
Good luck, please Google, Youtube or PM for any problems, don't clog the thread

> 
> NZDUSD H4 "Perfect" Double Top? {image} Trade well.

> Ignored

Nice chart, even a triple if you look back a little further, and now those points are last week's high.  
  
Now I have a suggestion for**Ensale** and others posting here, out of respect for the classical definition of Double Top & Double Bottom as defined by   
  
[https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double..._double_bottom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_top_and_double_bottom)  
  
I suggest that the shorter term patterns detected be labelled **Double Touch**(or Triple and so on) this will cover both highs & lows, no need for top & bottom.  
  
Or we could use Double Touch Support & Double Touch Resistance  
  
Because anyone coming here later will want to argue that these are not "true" tops & bottoms in the old fashioned definition  
  
That is, the very highest & lowest turning points on a large time frame eg. weeks & months.  
  
Your thoughts, good luck to all 

"Forex a Great Hobby, But Not a Great Job"

  * [#294](/thread/post/10209549#post10209549 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 21, 2017 10:34am  Aug 21, 2017 10:34am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar185229_8.gif) Erebus](erebus)

  * Joined Jul 2011 | Status: Trader | [8,577 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=185229)

> [Quoting frenchy.fx](/thread/post/10203890#post10203890 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> what is rwl?
> 
> Ignored

A question like this is usually ignored because no one can answer because there are no details or context provided.  
  
The only reason I am taking time to respond is because I recognize the "RWL" and I posted the indicator that prints that on whatever chart you seen it.  
  
**R** is for Range  
  
**W** is for Week and **D** is for Day  
  
**L** is for Low, conversely**H** is for High  
  
Not so hard is it?  
  
Basically an Average True Range that is projected from where the current High and Low are right now.  
  
These levels are dynamic with that indicator, which means they move depending on how far price is going in one direction.  
  
Once the Range is filled, the levels are fixed.  
  
If I remember, I will re-post this chart on Friday to see how the RWL and RWH looks then  
  
Good luck all

Why do you think it had died down?  
  
For me, the main thing, actually two main things, is understanding the differences between a DT/DB in a context of HH/LL or as a continuation.  
The second thing is to be disciplined which I'm working towards achieving.  
Sometimes I place a trade thinking "That's a DT/DB" and everything goes sideways from there and reverses on me, with a small account and too many trades or a SL placed too far, it means the end of the account (again ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) )  
  
  
I will share charts when I can but we're not allowed to upload images here at work and when I'm home I have little time to do anything other than packing these days but I'll do my best.  
  
  
Anyways, thanks for the DT/DB, I completely forgot about it till now.

If anyone want's the free version of bts, on tolis chart's.. here it is. .. below.. can be used for hourly and below. enjoy.  
  
HT1/LT1 Stands for 127.2 fib calculated based on previous day high / low.  
  
HT2/LT2 = 141.4 Fib  
  
H=High/long L=low/shortside

in the next candle after te gap it entered the light green "zone". Due to the gap can one short EU and close it when?  
  
Also should you put stops in general (I know it is subjective); based on HT1? at the lower end of the light green "zone" once trade initiated?  
  
Personally, I move sl to be once the candle has closed and then trail the lowest end of the previous candle and if it's a big one the previous candle I put the sl at the half of it.

I asked for Ensale's permission to post a M15 trade which I took on Friday. Looking at H4, the price closed as a pinbar, after there was a breakout, then pullback. I like setups when price breaks and then comes back to test the area, thus resistance becoming support, and viceversa. M15 showed DB with stop hunt, and my TP of 100 pips was almost hit in the same day, and it was Friday.

OK .. For simplicity sake.  
  
Going forward. have learned a lot from having the small group. since Fibonacci is a challenge to start with .. such as where do i draw the fib, do I use weekly, monthly etc. when do I use recent swing H/low.. question's like this can be eliminated by guiding you folk to only using one fib draw.. and that's from Previous day High and low, for all trading including 4HR.  
  
EUR/JPY example below. Each vertical represent's a new day.  
  
and for whatever trade trader's take. I suggest for them the 127.2 target. short side or long side. This approach is preferred for H1. But for 4HR trader's for now this is how I would like you to approach it.

Hi Catalin,  
  
I see the 1.50000 BRN Transitioning from Selling to Buying.   
  
Once all the Sell Orders have been consumed, at 1.50000, Buyers take their place and Price moves higher to find the next Level Selling.  
  
It's not necessarily a Stop Hunt.  
  
You are more likely to see a Stop Hunt Sweep a Double Top or Bottom because of the additional Stops placed there.

I have no idea where Price is going.  
  
The Institutions/Banks with the most Orders, either Long or Short, Consumes the Opposition and moves to the next Level of Liquidity for them to feed off.  
  
I have tried to Trade this way with some small success but the Institutions make it difficult for us to know where their Levels are.   
  
These days I tend to Trade all the Significant Levels.

  * [#364](/thread/post/10254301#post10254301 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 4, 2017 2:47am  Sep 4, 2017 2:47am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar164805_8.gif) stevepatt](stevepatt)

  * Joined Dec 2010 | Status: Never Stop Learning | [6,340 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=164805)

> [Quoting bistolis](/thread/post/10253620#post10253620 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> EURGBP DT 1H chart hit 200% (confluence of 38% retrace) {image}
> 
> Ignored

  
Hi Bistolis,  
  
We need to understand how Price gets moved by those who have the Money to do so.  
  
When Price has a Bullish Bias we will see Price get "run up" "they" then take some off (Profit) and "they" then Buy it back at a Lower Price.   
  
They keep doing this until they have no more to Buy, at this point they Sell everything and start to work Price into a Bearish Bias.  
  
We will now see Price get "run down" they will then take some off (Profit) and they then Sell it back at a Higher Price.  
  
They keep doing this until they have no more to Sell, at this point they Buy everything and start to work Price into a Bullish Bias.  
  
Along the way, of course, there are various Manipulations taking place to throw us of the scent.  
  
The clues, we have, are in where previous Transactions have taken place.  
  
Often Buying will Transition into Selling and Selling Transition into Buying.  
  
So its these Level where we need to be Anticipating being able to take Trades.  
  
A lot of the time we see significant Buying and Selling occurring at Whole and Half Numbers. 

Attached Image(s) (click to enlarge)

> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} Hi Bistolis, We need to understand how Price gets moved by those who have the Money to do so. When Price has a Bullish Bias we will see Price get "run up" "they" then take some off (Profit) and "they" then Buy it back at a Lower Price. They keep doing this until they have no more to Buy, at this point they Sell everything and start to work Price into a Bearish Bias. We will now see Price get "run down" they will then take some off (Profit) and they then Sell it back at a Higher Price. They keep doing this until they have no more to Sell,...
> 
> Ignored

Hi,  
  
Please, where can I learn to read the price like you just did with H1 EURGBP? 

How Can Mirrors Be Real If Our Eyes Aren't Real - Jaden Smith

here's what im looking for from particapant's   
  
1\. to be able to get on with people and work well with other's .  
  
2\. have one session (asia , london , US ) that they are able to trade, atleast 2/3 times a week. if there is a few that can trade asia and london your progress will be faster.  
  
3\. give yourself 3-6 month's to see if it suits you, within a week you'll see weather it's worth that, but practice of 3/6 months will reveal weather its has good potential for you, usually within this period trader will see some decent results , (inconsistent ) to carry on further then that.  
  
4\. lastly clean or cleaner mind, trader's that have attempted 10 different stratagies will have too much to unlearn or will mix approaches, we are looking for trader's that are 1/2 years in , perhaps have traded 2/3 basic strategies in the past.  
  
Goal is to not waste my time or your time... simple..  
  
wish you the best of luck

  * [#414](/thread/post/13140511#post13140511 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 31, 2020 10:37pm  Aug 31, 2020 10:37pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar355732_1.gif) ensale](ensale)

  * Joined Nov 2013 | Status: Trader | [2,780 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=355732)

OK, so I'm to explain core concepts that encover the whole FIBO/price action trading approach. What we try to practice and instill.  
  
1- Trend continution trades to probable consistent target. ( with price action )   
  
2- Trend continution to probable targets from deeper retracements.   
  
3- trading double tops/bottoms / trading retracements  
  
4- trading sfp, and some understanding of typical market trapping behaviours and tendencies.   
  
5- Trading 1.12 fib failure   
  
6- Trading to further targets once prime target is achieved  
  
  
mindset and risk  
  
1- self drive and seld reliance   
  
2- Proper riskM and mindset.   
  
3\. developing and research approach . always learning   
  
  
some challenges most will face -   
  
work trade and life balance, understanding and applying core concepts, finding their timeframe and approach . each trader will have to figure some aspects for themselves. 

It's in fear when people show what they truly value.

One example of one of the setup's  

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: Screenshot1.png
Size: 85 KB](/attachment/image/3729131/thumbnail?d=1598881335)](/attachment/image/3729131?d=1598881335)   

  
  
above example of 1.12 failure fib trade, so the trend fails to continue long and hit new areas (targets..) after several hit's its turns and breaks below the 20 ema, the entry is the red arrow, marked on the crossover of 20 ema (advanced trader's make a different entry)  
  
for this trade target is inside of previous day's action , 61.8 retrace is the conservative target typically. 

It's in fear when people show what they truly value.
